1.0 INTRODUCTION

This traffic study was conducted to evaluate the technical feasibility of converting 18th Street
between Blake Street and Wynkoop Street from one-way to two-way operation. This report
describes the major components of this study, including data collection, review of previous
planning documents relevant to this project, methods of traffic operation analysis, traffic
forecasts, development and evaluation of options, and determination of the preferred option.
The section of 18th Street under consideration for two-way conversion is located in downtown
Denver and consists of two blocks between Blake Street and Wynkoop Street, with Wazee
Street crossing in the middle. Figure 1 on the next page illustrates the study section of 18th
Street and a larger study area that includes one intersection on either side of the study
intersections. For the purpose of this study, numbered streets (17th, 18th, 19th, etc.) are referred
to as running in the north-south direction and named streets (Blake, Wazee, Wynkoop, etc.) in
the east-west direction.
This study focused on analyzing the potential impacts of the 18th Street one-way to two-way
conversion on multimodal transportation operations in the study area, identifying and
evaluating feasible options to mitigate traffic impacts, and developing traffic control strategies
for the two-way conversion.
The study team conducted extensive data collection and review, including field traffic counts,
supplemented by traffic data and previous planning/engineering documents furnished by the
City's Project Management Team (PMT). Traffic forecasts were developed using the Denver
Regional Council of Governments' (DRCOG) travel demand model, taking into account ongoing
and planned land use developments in and adjacent to the study area, particularly the Denver
Union Station (DUS) redevelopment project immediately northwest of the study area. The
study team used Synchro/SimTraffic traffic analysis and simulation software package to analyze
traffic operations under existing and future conditions. With input from the City's PMT and the
Regional Transportation District (RTD), the study team developed and evaluated various options
of geometric layout and traffic control strategies. As a result, a preferred option was identified
and recommended for converting 18th Street, between Blake Street and Wynkoop Street, from
one-way to two-way operation.

2.0 EXISTING CONDITIONS

This section describes the existing street network in the study area, including geometric
characteristics, traffic volumes, traffic operations, pedestrian and bicycle access, and parking
access on 18th Street.

2.1      Street Network
Figure 2 displays the layout of travel lanes and intersection turning lanes of 18th Street and
immediately adjacent or crossing streets in the study area. Eighteenth Street is currently a one-
way, northbound street. Between Wynkoop Street and Blake Street, both 17th Street and 19th
Street are two-way; they become one-way, southbound streets south of Blake Street. Wynkoop
Street and Wazee Street are two-way roads. Blake Street is one-way, westbound Street. Market
Street is a one-way, eastbound road.
                          Figure 2: Travel Lanes of the Street Network




Source: URS Corporation (Synchro snapshot)


Blake Street to Wynkoop Street                                                                     3
                                                                18th Street Two-Way Conversion Study

In addition to general-purpose travel lanes, 18th Street has a six-foot wide, northbound bike
lane which ends midway between Wazee Street and Wynkoop Street. Wynkoop Street also has
a six-foot bike lane in both directions.
All but two of the 12 intersections in the study area are controlled by a traffic signal. The
intersections of 17th Street/Wynkoop Street and 18th Street/Wynkoop Street are controlled by
all-way stop signs. Pedestrian signals are installed at all signalized intersections and pedestrian
crosswalks are striped at all intersections. All ten traffic signals in the study area are
coordinated as part of the downtown signal system through the Denver Traffic Management
Center.

2.2    Parking Access
On 18th Street, on-street meter parking is provided on one or both sides. From Market Street to
Blake Street, six on-street parking spaces are located on the east side of 18th Street. From Blake
Street to Wazee Street, eight on-street parking spaces are located on the west side and five on
the east side. From Wazee Street to Wynkoop Street, nine on-street parking spaces are located
on the west side and six on the east side. Mid-block driveways and alleys along 18th Street
provide access to several surface parking lots and parking structures on both sides of 18th
Street.
On-street parking, surface parking lots, and parking structures are also present on one or both
sides of other streets in the study area. The parking lane on the west side of 19th Street also
serves as a southbound High-Occupancy-Vehicle (HOV) lane during the morning peak periods (5
AM ­ 9 AM) on weekdays.

2.3    Existing Traffic Operations
To analyze traffic operations, the study team conducted AM and PM peak hour turning
movement counts (TMC) at three intersections on 18th Street ­ Wynkoop Street, Wazee Street,
and Blake Street (Appendix A) ­ in March 2013. TMC data for other intersections in the study
area were from historical traffic counts used in the 2010 Denver Central Business District (CBD)
Signal Retiming project. These historical TMC were then extrapolated into the current year
(2013) using growth factors derived from the DRCOG travel demand model and supplemental
daily traffic counts provided by the City (Appendix A). Figure 3 exhibits existing traffic volumes
in the study area.
Using the Synchro software, the study team analyzed existing traffic operations of all
intersections in the study area to establish the baseline conditions. The Highway Capacity
Manual (HCM) (Transportation Research Board [TRB], 2010) methodologies for intersection
evaluation were followed for this analysis. The performance measure used to describe the
quality of service for automobile traffic is level of service (LOS), expressed in a letter grade "A"
to "F", which is determined by the estimated average control delay per vehicle. LOS "A"
represents the most favorable operating conditions while "F" indicates severe congestion and
delay. The criteria for all-way-stop-controlled (AWSC) intersections have different threshold
values than those for signalized intersections. Table 1 illustrates the LOS criteria for both
signalized intersections and AWSC intersections.

operating conditions with low to moderate average control delay per vehicle. The Synchro
Reports in Appendix B consists of detailed input and output for capacity and LOS analysis.

3.0 TRAFFIC FORECASTS

For the purpose of evaluating options for 18th Street two-way conversion, year 2015 is
considered as the build year of the two-way conversion project and 2035 as the future design
year. The study team performed traffic forecasts of both future years under the no-build (18th
Street remains one-way) and build (18th Street is converted to two-way) conditions,
respectively. The multiple steps for developing the traffic forecasts are described below.
   1. The study team used the 2015 and 2035 DRCOG regional travel demand models to
      estimate the overall traffic growth for the study area. As results, AM peak hour volumes
      were estimated to increase by approximately 41% over the 20-year period; PM peak
      hour volumes were estimated to increase by 47%.
   2. Accordingly, the 2013 existing volumes were increased by 3.6% in the AM peak hour and
      3.8% in the PM peak hour to represent 2015 background traffic volumes under the no-
      build conditions. The word "background" means future traffic volumes accounting for
      regional traffic growth but excluding automobile traffic generated from the ongoing DUS
      development project.
   3. The 2015 background traffic volumes were then increased by 41% (AM peak) and 47%
      (PM peak) resulting in background traffic volumes in the 2035 AM and PM peak hours
      under the no-build conditions.
   4. To account for the impacts of the two-way conversion on vehicle circulations in the
      study area, the study team adjusted the above background traffic volumes to develop
      AM and PM peak hour volumes under the build (two-way 18th Street) conditions. These
      adjustments were made by assuming a portion of southbound traffic diverted from
      adjacent parallel streets, mainly 17th Street, onto 18th Street.
   5. Within the DUS development project area, the main terminal building and its North
      Wing and South Wing additions are the only buildings that will generate vehicle trips on
      the south side of DUS. The street network in the study area is not accessible for trips
      generated by properties on the north side of the DUS. Figure 4 on the next page
      illustrates the proposed street network in the DUS project area, as originally defined in
      the DUS Traffic Impact Study (TIS) (Navjoy, 2009).




Blake Street to Wynkoop Street                                                                   7

       and the forecast modal split associated with the DUS redevelopment. Table 3

4.0 DEVELOPMENT AND EVALUATION OF OPTIONS

This section describes the process of identifying and screening various options for 18th Street
one-way to two-way conversion, establishing the Preferred Option, and the general benefits
and impacts of the Preferred Option.

4.1    Options for Two-Way Conversion
To identify viable options for 18th Street one-way to two-way conversion, the study team took
into account the following factors that determine the feasibility of two-way conversion:
   1. The right-of-way and pavement width (curb to curb) will remain unchanged. From Blake
      Street to Wynkoop Street, 18th Street currently has a curb-to-curb pavement width of
      approximately 48 feet including on-street parking lanes on both sides.
   2. To provide convenient parking access for downtown businesses and visitors, the City
      prefers to preserve on-street parking spaces to the maximum extent.
   3. Direct access to midblock parking lots, parking garages, alleys, and loading areas along
      18th Street need to be provided.
   4. The existing bike lane on 18th Street, which ends midblock between Wazee Street and
      Wynkoop Street, will remain or be extended.
   5. One of the initial motives for the 18th Street two-way conversion is to provide better
      transit connection that the City identified between the DUS and the rest of downtown.
      The City is willing to consider converting part of 18th Street southbound to bus-only
      operation.
   6. According to an agreement between the City and RTD, a new Downtown Circulator bus
      route will have a northbound transit stop with a raised bus bulb on 18th Street near
      Wazee Street. This bus bulb will be 10.5 feet wide and located within the current street
      right-of-way. Figure 10 illustrates the layout of the bus bulb.
With the above considerations, the study team developed the following distinctive two-way
conversion options for further screening analysis:
   1. Southbound 18th Street from Wynkoop Street to Blake Street will be bus only ­ other
      automobile traffic will be prohibited from traveling southbound on 18th Street.
   2. Allow all vehicular modes (buses, passenger cars, bicycles, etc.) to travel in both
      directions on 18th Street. The RTD bus stop with in-street bus bulb will be located on
      18th Street south (i.e., near side) of Wazee Street.
   3. Allow all vehicular modes to travel in both directions on 18th Street. The RTD bus stop
      with in-street bus bulb will be located on 18th Street south (i.e., near side) of Wynkoop
      Street.
   4. Allow all vehicular modes to travel in both directions on 18th Street. The RTD bus stop
      with in-street bus bulb will be located on 18th Street north (i.e., far side) of Wazee
      Street.


Blake Street to Wynkoop Street                                                                    15
                                                                            Figure 10: RTD Bus Bulb on 18th Street




Blake Street to Wynkoop Street
                                                                                                                     18th Street Two-Way Conversion Study




     16

4.2    Screening of Options
The screening of the above options used criteria including impacts on traffic operations, traffic
safety, parking access, impacts on utilities, and cost. The following paragraphs briefly describe
the screening process and results.
Option 1 (bus only southbound on 18th Street) would require removal of one or more (for turn
lanes) northbound lanes in order to provide a southbound transit lane and a turn lane, where
necessary, at intersections. The existing bike lane would remain or be extended to Wynkoop
Street. Some of the on-street parking spaces would have to be removed to make room for
bidirectional travel, turn lanes, and the RTD bus bulb. This option was eliminated mainly
because: (1) it would not provide two-way operation for the general traffic; (2) intersection
capacity and level of service on 18th Street would deteriorate due to reduced number of
northbound lanes; and (3) the benefits of providing southbound transit connection for two
blocks on 18th Street do not justify the costs and impacts on traffic operations.
Option 2 would allow all vehicles to travel in either direction on 18th Street. The proposed RTD
northbound bus stop with an in-street bus bulb would be installed on the south side (near side)
of Wazee Street. The existing bike lane would remain or be extended to Wynkoop Street. Some
of the existing on-street parking would be removed. This option includes a near-side bus stop;
however, RTD prefers a far-side bus stop. Only one northbound lane would remain to carry all
turning movements at Wazee Street, causing over-capacity and a LOS "F" during the PM peak
hour in 2035. Therefore, this option is screened out from further consideration.
Option 3 would allow all vehicles to travel in either direction on 18th Street. The proposed RTD
northbound bus stop with an in-street bus bulb would be installed on the south side (near side)
of Wynkoop Street. The existing bike would remain or be extended to Wynkoop Street. Some of
the existing on-street parking would be removed. Similar to Option 2, this option includes a
near-side bus stop, while RTD prefers a far-side bus stop. In addition, the raised in-street bus
bulb would cause drainage issues because of the grades at this intersection and the current
inlet is located at the southeastern corner. Therefore, this option is eliminated.
Option 4 would allow all vehicles to travel in either direction on 18th Street. The proposed RTD
northbound bus stop with an in-street bus bulb would be installed on 18th Street north (far side)
of Wazee Street. The existing bike lane would remain or be extended to Wynkoop Street. Some
of the existing on-street parking would be removed. Compared with Options 2 and 3, this
option meets RTD's preference of having a far-side bus stop and avoids the drainage issues. This
option was considered as the Preferred Option and is illustrated in Figure 11.

                                                                                                  18th Street Two-Way Conversion Study

4.3    Preferred Option
This subsection describes key components of the Preferred Option and presents a concept-level
cost estimate for implementing the Preferred Option.
Street and Intersection Geometry
As illustrated in Figure 11, 18th Street will consist of one general-purpose travel lane in each
direction between Blake Street and Wynkoop Street. In addition, an exclusive northbound left-
turn lane will be installed at Wazee Street and at Wynkoop Street, respectively. A northbound
right-turn pocket will be maintained at Wazee Street. The southbound travel lane will become
right-turn only at Blake Street, so that 18th Street will remain one-way northbound south of
Blake Street.
As illustrated in Figure 10, the northbound RTD bus bulb will be located immediately north of
Wazee Street. To avoid vehicles getting trapped in the intersection behind a stopped bus, a
second northbound travel lane is provided from Wazee Street to Wynkoop Street. The
northbound bike lane could be extended to Wynkoop Street, as shown in Figure 11, or end
midblock north of Wazee Street, as it currently does.
Approximately nine to 13 of the 28 existing on-street parking spaces will need to be eliminated
to provide for bidirectional travel and turn lanes. In addition, construction of the RTD bus bulb
would require removal of two to three on-street parking spaces.
Intersection Traffic Control
The Denver Union Station Final Environmental Impact Statement (FEIS) (RTD, 2008) indicated
that a traffic signal at the intersection of 18th Street and Wynkoop Street was warranted.
Accordingly, the City made the decision to construct a traffic signal at this intersection with the
two-way conversion. The URS study team determined that this intersection meets the Manual
of Uniform Traffic Control Devices (MUTCD 2009) Traffic Signal Warrant 6 ­ Coordinated Signal
System, and is expected to meet Warrant 3 ­ Peak Hour ­ and Warrant 6 in 2035. The Highway
Capacity Software (HCS 2010) Reports in Appendix C consists of detailed information on these
warrant checks. Since the volume of pedestrians crossing this intersection is expected to
increase substantially after the DUS redevelopment project is complete, a traffic signal with
pedestrian signal heads at this intersection would improve traffic safety. Traffic analysis reveals
that compared with the current all-way stop control, a traffic signal would reduce delay and
improve the intersection LOS from "C" to "B".
The existing traffic signals on 18th Street at Wazee Street and Blake Street will be reconstructed
to accommodate southbound movements. The traffic signal at 18th Street and Blake Street
requires special attention due to relatively high turning volumes, pedestrians crossing Blake
Street on the west side of 18th Street facing conflicts with multiple vehicular turning
movements (westbound through, southbound right turn, and northbound left-turn), and RTD
buses from 18th southbound onto Blake westbound having to cross two lanes to be ready for
the next left turn at 17th Street. Figure 12 illustrates the proposed phasing and movement
diagram for the intersection of 18th Street at Blake Street. Figure 13 displays the proposed
phasing splits for this intersection. The cycle length of all traffic signals is assumed to remain at
90 seconds.

Blake Street to Wynkoop Street                                                                     19
                                                               18th Street Two-Way Conversion Study

        Figure 12: Proposed Phasing/Movement Diagram at 18th Street and Blake Street

As shown in Figures 12 and 13, phase 2 provides for northbound through movement on 18th
Street, phase 4 provides for westbound through and right-turn movement on Blake Street,
phase 5 provides for northbound left-turn movement on 18th Street, and phase 6 provides for
southbound right-turn movement on 18th Street. Phase 9 provides a head start for southbound
right turn movement, during which no conflicting vehicle or pedestrian movement is allowed.
Similarly, phase 10 provides a head start for pedestrians crossing Blake Street on the west side
of 18th Street, during which no vehicle movement that conflicts with crossing pedestrians is
allowed.

         4. Under the Build condition, a westbound left-turn pocket is assumed to be installed on Wynkoop at 17 Street.

The following observations were made based on the performance measures shown in Table 4:
        1. In the 2015 No-Build (i.e., 18th Street remains one-way) and Build (Preferred Option)
           conditions, all study intersections are expected to operate at LOS "C" or better. There is
           no significant operational difference between the No-Build and Build conditions.
        2. In 2035, all but one study intersections are expected to operate at LOS "D" or better
           under the No-Build and Build conditions. There is no significant operational difference
           between the No-Build and Build conditions. The intersection of 17th and Wynkoop is
           expected to have a LOS "F" under No-Build and LOS "E" under the Build conditions. By
           installing a westbound left-turn pocket, the LOS would be improved to LOS "D" under
           the Build conditions.



Blake Street to Wynkoop Street                                                                                            21
                                                                                 18th Street Two-Way Conversion Study

    3. In general, converting 18th Street, Blake to Wynkoop, from one-way to two-way is
       expected to provide similar or slightly better traffic operations in the study area.
Transit Operations
The planned RTD bus routes on 18th Street include the Downtown Circulator, Route 0 (existing),
and Route 15 Limited (15L, existing). Figure 14 displays the planned Downtown Circulator
route. In the current plan, the outbound (southbound) portion of the three planned RTD routes
will not travel on 18th Street, but instead will use 17th Street (Route 0 and 15L) and 19th Street
(Downtown Circulator). With the 18th Street two-way conversion, the City and RTD desires to
explore the feasibility of moving these routes onto 18th Street. Figure 15 illustrates alternate
outbound (southbound) routes versus the three planned routes. Route #1 is the outbound
portion of the Downtown Circulator; Route #1-A represents an alternate outbound route of the
Downtown Circulator, which travels southbound on 18th Street; Route #2 is the outbound
portion of Route 0 and 15L; and Route #2-A is an alternate outbound route of Route 0 and 15L
traveling southbound on 18th Street.
Table 5 summarizes operation analysis results of the above four transit routes for the No-Build
(18th Street remains one-way) and Build (Preferred Option) conditions in 2015 and 2035. The
following observations were made based on the performance measure (average travel speed)
values shown in Table 5:
    1. The two-way conversion of 18th Street is expected to maintain RTD bus operations, as
       the planned Downtown Circulator (Route #1 in Table 5) and Routes 0 and 15L (Route #2
       in Table 5) are estimated to have similar average travel speeds under the No-Build
       compared with the Build conditions.
    2. Under the Build conditions, an alternate route for the Downtown Circulator (Route #1-A,
       traveling southbound on 18th Street) is expected to have a higher travel speed than the
       currently planned route (Route #1); similarly, an alternate route for RTD Bus Route 0
       and 15L (Route #2-A, traveling southbound on 18th Street) is expected to have a higher
       travel speed than the currently planned route (Route #2).

Table 5: Future Year Bus Travel Speeds ­ No-Build and Build Conditions

 Route #1-A          N/A           N/A          11.6          11.5         N/A           N/A          9.3           10.4
 Route #2            6.2           7.0          6.6           7.2          5.4           4.9          5.5           5.6

Concept-Level Cost Estimate
The study team conducted a concept-level estimate of the construction costs for the Preferred
Option, which is summarized in Appendix D. The estimated total cost is approximately
$1,365,000.




Blake Street to Wynkoop Street                                                               24
                                                             18th Street Two-Way Conversion Study

5.0 CONCLUSIONS

This study analyzed the technical feasibility of converting 18th Street, Blake to Wynkoop, from
one-way to two-way operations. The study team identified and evaluated various options of
two-way conversion in comparison with the No-Build (one-way) conditions. A Preferred Option
was identified as the most beneficial and feasible option for the two-way conversion.
The study team recommends that the Preferred Option, as described in Section 4, be
implemented by Year 2015. A traffic signal should be installed at the intersection of 18th Street
and Wynkoop Street to replace the existing all-way stop signs. A westbound left-turn lane of 50
feet or longer on Wynkoop Street at 17th Street should be installed to improve LOS from "E" to
"D" (2035). North of Wazee Street, a second northbound travel lane on 18th Street should be
installed so that vehicles can bypass a stopped bus at the far side bus stop. No other mitigation
measures appear necessary. The study team recommends that RTD consider alternate routes
for the Downtown Circulator, Route 0 and 15L to use 18th Street for outbound (southbound)
travel as they appear to offer higher travel speeds.
